    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13806141270084074572">Winner of the Nobel Prize for Literature in 1909  — the first woman to be so honored — Swedish novelist Selma Lagerlöf (1858–1940) was a gifted storyteller whose writings were often tinged with the supernatural and rooted in the sagas and legends of her homeland.<br/>She secured her reputation as a children's-book author with  <i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i>, long considered a</span>
  <span id="freeText13806141270084074572" style="display:none">Winner of the Nobel Prize for Literature in 1909  — the first woman to be so honored — Swedish novelist Selma Lagerlöf (1858–1940) was a gifted storyteller whose writings were often tinged with the supernatural and rooted in the sagas and legends of her homeland.<br />She secured her reputation as a children's-book author with  <i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i>, long considered a masterpiece of children's literature. Written at the request of Swedish school authorities and first published in 1906, it is the enchanting and remarkably original tale of Nils Holgersson, a mischievous boy of 14 who is changed by an elf into a tiny being able to understand the speech of birds and animals.<br />Brilliantly weaving fact and fiction into a breathtaking and beautiful fable, the story recounts Nils's adventures as he is transported over the countryside on the back of a goose. From this vantage point, Nils witnesses a host of events that provide young readers with an abundance of information about nature, geography, folklore, animal life, and more.<br />Reset in easy-to-read type and enhanced with 10 new illustrations, this inexpensive, unabridged edition will bring new generations of readers under the magical spell of a timeless classic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13806141270084074572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=nobels">nobels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976564310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11309768847054449946">Cross-curricular teaching and entertainment in one Nobel volume.<br/><br/>These days, interdisciplinary projects and cross-curricular interlinking of learning are all the fashion, and stressed teachers sigh in frustration over the tour de force of teaching not only their own subject, but of successfully implementing relevant connections to other areas as well in order to make learning more meaningful to an increasingly lazy, naughty and careless student body.<br/> <br/>Some might think this is a recent issue - both</span>
  <span id="freeText11309768847054449946" style="display:none">Cross-curricular teaching and entertainment in one Nobel volume.<br><br>These days, interdisciplinary projects and cross-curricular interlinking of learning are all the fashion, and stressed teachers sigh in frustration over the tour de force of teaching not only their own subject, but of successfully implementing relevant connections to other areas as well in order to make learning more meaningful to an increasingly lazy, naughty and careless student body.<br> <br>Some might think this is a recent issue - both the emphasis on interdisciplinary learning, and the hopeless attitude of our youth. Think again - or read Selma Lagerlöf, and you will be pleased to discover that: <br><br>a) your interdisciplinary project combining a learning unit in geography, biology, history, literature, ethics, Nordic mythology and life skills is offered to you on a Nobel silver plate.<br><br>b) students have been lazy, naughty and prone to falling asleep over their chores or homework at least since 1906, when this novel was written to be used in the Swedish school system.<br><br>Following young Nils Holgersson on his magical journey through the various landscapes of Sweden is a special experience, as it combines features of a fairy tale adventure with genuine geography and biology knowledge. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505407226i/23923408._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nils is cursed by a Swedish house spirit, a"tomte", for his cruel and treacherous behaviour, and is turned into a a tiny "tomte" himself. Deprived of his physical superiority, he faces the animals on his parents' farm, whom he has treated in a particularly nasty way. He discovers that he has received the ability to understand their communication as a compensation for his lost power, and he has to hear some unpleasant opinions about himself, as well as protect himself against the mistreated animals' righteous anger. <br><br>Fleeing the farm on the back of a goose, he travels through all of Sweden. The journey widens his perspective and broadens his mind, and the hardship he faces makes him grow as a human being, -<br> despite or because of his tiny size. He learns to respect nature and living creatures by slowly gaining deeper understanding of the diversity of lifeforms in Sweden. <br><br>He returns home more caring and knowledgeable, and vows to be a better leader of the environment for which he is responsible. The curse is gone, and he resumes his human shape.<br><br>Apart from the purely subject-related content, offering a panorama of Swedish flora and fauna, it is a universal story of power and responsibility, and of the importance of knowledge to develop empathy. To respect others, you need to know about their situation, and about their needs and feelings and customs.<br><br>Recommended to teachers, students and learners for life!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11309768847054449946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1610995245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610995245" />
    <a title="Manny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1713956-manny"><img alt="Manny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1610995245?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manny" href="/user/show/1713956-manny">Manny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/29919857-nils-holgerssons-wunderbare-reise">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who appreciate classic children's stories</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Manny by: </span>
      About a quarter of Sweden
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=german-and-dutch">german-and-dutch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=swedish-norwegian-and-danish">swedish-norwegian-and-danish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1610995245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17969566452026774865">This children's classic, published in 1906 by future Nobel Prize winner Selma Lagerlöf, is so famous in Scandinavia that everyone knows the plot; but until now I'd never read it. Nils Holgersson, a good-for-nothing kid in late nineteenth century Skåne, angers the local <i>tomte</i> (a kind of Swedish leprechaun), who magically transforms him into another <i>tomte</i>. Nils, who's now the size of a thumb, is fortunately adopted by a flock of geese who take him to their summer nesting grounds in Lapland and bac</span>
  <span id="freeText17969566452026774865" style="display:none">This children's classic, published in 1906 by future Nobel Prize winner Selma Lagerlöf, is so famous in Scandinavia that everyone knows the plot; but until now I'd never read it. Nils Holgersson, a good-for-nothing kid in late nineteenth century Skåne, angers the local <i>tomte</i> (a kind of Swedish leprechaun), who magically transforms him into another <i>tomte</i>. Nils, who's now the size of a thumb, is fortunately adopted by a flock of geese who take him to their summer nesting grounds in Lapland and back again. En route, they conveniently traverse all of Sweden, giving the author ample opportunity for an extended series of geography lessons. It sounded dull, but I was pleased to discover that in fact it's nothing of the kind. The geography is always firmly in the service of the narrative, the lead characters are well drawn, and the style is moving and poetic. But what surprised me most was that I'd never heard how it came to be written.<br /><br />According to the introduction, the author's original inspiration was a terrible story she had heard from her grandmother about an incident that had occurred when the grandmother was herself a little girl. There was a white goose on the farm, and one spring day he took it into his head to fly off with a flock of wild geese who were passing by. The family was of course sure they would never see him again. But many months later, Selma's grandmother was astonished to see that the goose had returned. And he was not alone; during the summer, he had found a mate, a beautiful grey goose, and they were accompanied by half a dozen little goslings. Delighted, Selma's grandmother led the goose family to the barn, where they could eat from the trough with the other fowl. She closed the door so that they wouldn't fly off again, and ran to tell her stepmother. The stepmother said nothing. She just took out the little knife she used for slaughtering geese; and an hour later there was not one goose left alive in the barn. <br /><br />For me, this resonated with what many other people also find the most memorable episode in the book. One night, Nils is woken by a stork, who says that if he follows him he will show him something important. They fly to the seashore, where there is a strange city, quite unlike anything one would expect to find on the Swedish coast. Nils goes in through the huge gate and discovers people dressed in rich clothes from a bygone age. No one seems to notice him at first. He finds his way to the merchants' quarter. People are selling all kinds of precious goods: embroidered silks and satins, gold ornaments, glittering jewels. And now he realizes that the merchants can see him. They are holding out their wares to him, offering all these treasures. Nils tries to make them understand that he could never afford any of it, he is a poor boy. But they persist, and using gestures tell him that he can have anything he wants, if he can just give them one small copper coin. He searches his pockets over and over again but finds they are empty. In the end, he leaves the city, and when he turns round again it has disappeared. "It is the lost city of the sea traders," explains the stork. "They were drowned beneath the waves long ago, but once every hundred years they come back for a single night. The legend is that if they can sell a single thing to a mortal, they will be allowed to return to the world; but they never do." Nils feels his heart is going to break. He could so easily have saved all these good people and their city, but he has failed them.<br /><br />It seemed to me that both stories expressed the same feeling with quite unusual clarity. If only...<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17969566452026774865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The talking animal surpass those of Kipling's Jungle Book in detail and characterization, and they are also talking about such subjects like deforestation and industrialisation. And there is additional flavour of histories, local folktales and legends.</span>

<div id="review_1674734649" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674734649?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780241206089" href="/book/show/29777025-the-wonderful-adventure-of-nils-holgersson">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674734649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6693234050007899126">“The Wonderful Adventure of Nils Holgersson,” is a Swedish children’s classic. Published in 1906, the book actually resulted from a commission from the National Teachers Association to write a geography reader. Author Selma Lagerlof apparently spent three years studying Nature and also investigating folklore and legends from around the country, before writing this book.<br/><br/>The story itself involves a fourteen year old boy called Nils who is a bit lazy and naughty. Amongst the mischief he gets up to </span>
  <span id="freeText6693234050007899126" style="display:none">“The Wonderful Adventure of Nils Holgersson,” is a Swedish children’s classic. Published in 1906, the book actually resulted from a commission from the National Teachers Association to write a geography reader. Author Selma Lagerlof apparently spent three years studying Nature and also investigating folklore and legends from around the country, before writing this book.<br /><br />The story itself involves a fourteen year old boy called Nils who is a bit lazy and naughty. Amongst the mischief he gets up to is the rather unpleasant way he likes to hurt animals on his family farm. One day, he is left home to memorise Bible chapters and then falls asleep. Waking, he sees a gnome, which he traps. Eventually, he is also turned into a gnome and able to talk to animals. With wild geese flying over the farm, a farm goose attempts to fly off with them and, when Nils grabs hold, the two of them end up on an adventure…<br /><br />This book involves a lot of the history and natural world of Sweden, which is a beautiful country. At just over 270 pages and with an illustration at the beginning of each chapter, this is certainly a book for the more fluent child reader; although it is also delightful to read aloud. It has a lovely, hardback cover, with pictures of flying geese and is an unusual story. It reminded me a little of BB and his, “The Little Grey Men go Down the Bright Stream,” if not in the actual storyline, but in the way the countryside and natural beauty was so integral to the book. A lovely novel for adults and children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6693234050007899126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1653379307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1653379307" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39972744-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437513165p2/39972744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1653379307?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/39972744-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789148506094" href="/book/show/469808.Nils_Holgerssons_underbara_resa_genom_Sverige">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39972744-leah?shelf=children-literature">children-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39972744-leah?shelf=scandinavian">scandinavian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1653379307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer207979568182825110">This book will give you so much. <br/>How is it that Swedish writers always find the right words for expressing children's thoughts and feelings? Lagerlöf does a great job, not only in describing the Swedish landscape, but also in describing and telling Nils' story. It is a wonderful piece of literature and should be read to every child. <br/>You can learn a lot from Nils Holgersson. It deals with topics different to speak about, like death, sickness or growing up. And while writing about it in such a uni</span>
  <span id="freeText207979568182825110" style="display:none">This book will give you so much. <br />How is it that Swedish writers always find the right words for expressing children's thoughts and feelings? Lagerlöf does a great job, not only in describing the Swedish landscape, but also in describing and telling Nils' story. It is a wonderful piece of literature and should be read to every child. <br />You can learn a lot from Nils Holgersson. It deals with topics different to speak about, like death, sickness or growing up. And while writing about it in such a unique manner, she manages to teach children values like friendship and trust. <br />Absolutely adored it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="207979568182825110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168395059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168395059" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666282-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556719821p2/666282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168395059?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/666282-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781572160361" href="/book/show/192748.Nils">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168395059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13787384814784642295">I was about 10 years old, and looking for something to read on a quiet Sunday afternoon in summer, when I ran across a battered and faded copy of The Wonderful Adventures of Nils. Originally published in Sweden in 1906-7, it tells the story of a naughty farmer's lad who has what we would today call attitude, toward his parents, toward farming, and toward the animals on the farm. He's a terror, in short, and his parents despair of him. An elf turns him into a tiny version of himself (just go with</span>
  <span id="freeText13787384814784642295" style="display:none">I was about 10 years old, and looking for something to read on a quiet Sunday afternoon in summer, when I ran across a battered and faded copy of The Wonderful Adventures of Nils. Originally published in Sweden in 1906-7, it tells the story of a naughty farmer's lad who has what we would today call attitude, toward his parents, toward farming, and toward the animals on the farm. He's a terror, in short, and his parents despair of him. An elf turns him into a tiny version of himself (just go with it), and he's nearly eaten, crushed, or lost hundreds of times on his subsequent journeys around Sweden in the company of a marvelous flock of geese. <br /><br />Of course he learns wonderful lessons along the way, about himself, the animals and birds that suddenly loom much larger in his life, and the land he travels through. Lagerlof was an early environmentalist, as well as an intellectual with theories about bringing up children, and a deep knowledge of Sweden's geography. <br /><br />I was entranced, and tore through the book on that long, rainy afternoon. Then, over the years, I forgot about Nils, until a combination of Sunday, rain, and the search for a good book brought back a faint memory. Google did the rest, and I was delighted to find that the book is still in print, though hardly a bestseller.<br /><br />Too bad. It's quite brilliant, and while it was originally written to teach Swedish schoolchildren about geography, the descriptions of the places never get in the way of a good story. It's perfect for your 8 - 10 year old's bedtime reading aloud, though be warned that it contains real peril, death, and something of an education in the hard life of people making a living from the land. It's a book to raise your child's sights, imagination, and IQ. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13787384814784642295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319419726" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitha Murthy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitha Murthy" href="/user/show/3547543-smitha-murthy">Smitha Murthy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18880657-the-wonderful-adventures-of-nils">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=women-writers">women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3547543-smitha-murthy?shelf=read-with-jo">read-with-jo</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319419726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5264615529055960349">There’s so much to the world of reading, sigh. And I continue to explore more aspects of Children’s Literature. In ‘The Wonderful Adventures of Nils,’ Selma Lagerlof has created a slow, mindful book that draws you into a world of adventure, fun, and learning. Initially, I found the pace of the book a bit slow, and thought it might be boring. But I caught myself just in time - we are usd to fast-paced action thriller of novels - we are not used to ‘mindful’ novels. This is one of those. <br/><br/>This book</span>
  <span id="freeText5264615529055960349" style="display:none">There’s so much to the world of reading, sigh. And I continue to explore more aspects of Children’s Literature. In ‘The Wonderful Adventures of Nils,’ Selma Lagerlof has created a slow, mindful book that draws you into a world of adventure, fun, and learning. Initially, I found the pace of the book a bit slow, and thought it might be boring. But I caught myself just in time - we are usd to fast-paced action thriller of novels - we are not used to ‘mindful’ novels. This is one of those. <br /><br />This book invites you to just sit back with a cup of tea and fall in love with Thumbietot and Goosey-Gander, marvel at Sweden’s gorgeous landscape described so poetically by Lagerlof, and just think of reading the way it would have been before smartphones and the Internet bombarded us with shortened attention spans.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974924418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17652655146557989732">Sometimes its the perspective of a child that gives adults much needed clarity. Without hyperbole, metaphors or euphemisms, this wonderful tale of adventure manages to show the complexity of nature and the abuse nature has gone through in the hands of humans. Selma Lagerlöf writes story about a boy who isn't always very nice and one day annoys an elf enough to get himself hit by a spell - the boy, Nils, can now understand animals and birds along with turning into a very tiny person. He travels a</span>
  <span id="freeText17652655146557989732" style="display:none">Sometimes its the perspective of a child that gives adults much needed clarity. Without hyperbole, metaphors or euphemisms, this wonderful tale of adventure manages to show the complexity of nature and the abuse nature has gone through in the hands of humans. Selma Lagerlöf writes story about a boy who isn't always very nice and one day annoys an elf enough to get himself hit by a spell - the boy, Nils, can now understand animals and birds along with turning into a very tiny person. He travels across the country (Sweden) on the back of a gander and understands the nature through the eyes of birds.<br /><br /><i>Thw wonderful adventures of Nils</i> is definitely one of the best books I've read this year.</span>

<div id="review_2453766072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2453766072" />
    <a title="Swati" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2992522-swati"><img alt="Swati" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554291691p2/2992522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2453766072?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Swati" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Swati" href="/user/show/2992522-swati">Swati</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2453766072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer233656030738206007">The Wonderful Adventures of Nils is very unlike many of the other children's classics that I have read in recent times. For one, it moves slowly. Sometimes tiresomely so. But after a point you realize that the slowness allows you to take in every detail that Selma Lagerlof lays out for you much like the aerial views that Nils is treated to when he rides with the geese above the clouds. <br/><br/>Lagerlof weaves in many delightful Swedish folktales into Nils' adventures, which add great flavour and colour.</span>
  <span id="freeText233656030738206007" style="display:none">The Wonderful Adventures of Nils is very unlike many of the other children's classics that I have read in recent times. For one, it moves slowly. Sometimes tiresomely so. But after a point you realize that the slowness allows you to take in every detail that Selma Lagerlof lays out for you much like the aerial views that Nils is treated to when he rides with the geese above the clouds. <br /><br />Lagerlof weaves in many delightful Swedish folktales into Nils' adventures, which add great flavour and colour. One of the most impressionable ones for me was where Nils encounters a ghostly town populated by rich, garishly dressed locals. He moves around and is astonished to find people offering him expensive items in exchange for a coin. Later, he comes to know that it is a city that disappeared because of its greed. It comes alive for an hour every year where the residents have a chance to reclaim their reality if someone buys something for a coin. <br /><br />This is just one of the many moralistic fables that Lagerlof intersperses the picaresque narrative with. At the end of this grand and epic journey, Nils has grown up beyond his years. From being an indifferent and cruel boy who hurt animals he transforms into a sensitive and kind individual. A very telling episode that illustrates the huge change in Nils is when he runs to Morten Goosy Gander's rescue, towards the end, without regard for himself.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book with its extensive descriptions of the lush Swedish landscape, and its story-within-a-story format. A lovely novel for all ages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="233656030738206007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1444713206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1444713206" />
    <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca"><img alt="Manuel Alfonseca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420279369p2/35970992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1444713206?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Alfonseca" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca">Manuel Alfonseca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444713206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14222590896564308130">ENGLISH: This was one of my favorite books during my early adolescence. To practice French, my uncle Felipe gave me a copy of Nils translated into that language, which I proceeded to translate into Spanish during the next two summers (at the age of 12 and 13). I still have the pages where I wrote the translated text. Apart from some mischief, like systematically translating "oie" by "duck" ("goose" sounded bad to me), the translation is quite acceptable.<br/><br/>This is the seventh time I've read this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText14222590896564308130" style="display:none">ENGLISH: This was one of my favorite books during my early adolescence. To practice French, my uncle Felipe gave me a copy of Nils translated into that language, which I proceeded to translate into Spanish during the next two summers (at the age of 12 and 13). I still have the pages where I wrote the translated text. Apart from some mischief, like systematically translating "oie" by "duck" ("goose" sounded bad to me), the translation is quite acceptable.<br /><br />This is the seventh time I've read this book, the first in English translation, because I've usually read it in French or Spanish (including my own). Every time I've read it, I've found something new, and I'm amazed at the author's literary abilities. She, by the way, introduced herself as an unnamed character in her own work.<br /><br />Given that this book was published in 1906 and 1907, and that each chapter is dated with the day of the week, the day and the month, but not with the year, I have been able to deduce that the year when Nils Holgersson toured Sweden on the back of a white goose was 1904.<br /><br />Reading Nils led me to become interested in other works by Selma Lagerlöf, which although I didn't like as much as Nils, I found satisfactory: "The story of Gösta Berling" and the collections of stories titled "Invisible links" and "Christ's legends".<br /><br />ESPAÑOL: Este fue uno de mis libros favoritos durante mi primera adolescencia. Para que practicara el francés, mi tío Felipe me regaló un ejemplar de Nils traducido a esa lengua, que procedí a traducir al español durante los dos veranos siguientes (a la edad de 12 y 13 años). Todavía conservo las cuartillas donde escribí el texto traducido. Aparte de alguna pifia, como traducir sistemáticamente "oie" por "pato" (lo de "ganso" me sonaba mal), la traducción es bastante aceptable.<br /><br />Esta es la séptima vez que leo este libro, la primera en traducción inglesa, porque usualmente lo he leído en francés o en español (incluida mi propia traducción). Cada vez que lo leo, me descubre algo nuevo y me asombra la habilidad literaria de la autora, que incluso se introdujo como personaje (aunque sin nombrarse) en su propia obra.<br /><br />Teniendo en cuenta que este libro se publicó en 1906 y 1907, y que cada capítulo está fechado con el día de la semana, el día y el mes, pero no con el año, he podido deducir que el año en que Nils Holgersson recorrió toda Suecia a lomos de un ganso blanco fue el 1904.<br /><br />Leer Nils me condujo a interesarme por otras obras de Selma Lagerlöf, que aunque no me gustaron tanto como esta, sí me resultaron satisfactorias, como "La saga de Gösta Berling" y las colecciones de cuentos tituladas, "Los lazos invisibles" y "Leyendas de Cristo".<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14222590896564308130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was originally commissioned by the National Teachers Association as a geography reader for the public schools. I wish the American school s</span>

It was originally commissioned by the National Teachers Association as a geography reader for the public schools. I wish the American school system did stuff like that.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5487395353204132020">As the author wrote this with an emphasis on the geography of Sweden, some portions of each chapter were a bit slow and dry. Mama wants to get back to reading Ralph Moody's series aloud.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12743436852910767039">It is a lovely story.<br/>Nils is a young boy who is a real a-hole. He is mean to everyone, especially animals, he is lazy, stubborn, full of mischief... then one day he's mean to a wrong person, and becomes a gnome.<br/>This is the story of his summer with the wild geese, flying from Southern Sweden to Northern and then back again. There are many adventures during the journey, and many stories. This book talks about the importance of being kind to your fellow beings (especially animals), about nature and</span>
  <span id="freeText12743436852910767039" style="display:none">It is a lovely story.<br />Nils is a young boy who is a real a-hole. He is mean to everyone, especially animals, he is lazy, stubborn, full of mischief... then one day he's mean to a wrong person, and becomes a gnome.<br />This is the story of his summer with the wild geese, flying from Southern Sweden to Northern and then back again. There are many adventures during the journey, and many stories. This book talks about the importance of being kind to your fellow beings (especially animals), about nature and caring for nature, about love of father's land; it's a beautiful description of Sweden. <br />Selma writes in a very engaging manner and it's easy to read.<br />I love the end. Even though it was very sad, it was also very lovely. I'm sitting here crying and smiling at the same time. </span>

<div id="review_1156865436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156865436" />
    <a title="Craig Barner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20603605-craig-barner"><img alt="Craig Barner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369426424p2/20603605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156865436?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig Barner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig Barner" href="/user/show/20603605-craig-barner">Craig Barner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20603605-craig-barner?shelf=20th-century-lit">20th-century-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20603605-craig-barner?shelf=children-s-lit">children-s-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20603605-craig-barner?shelf=fantasy-and-romance">fantasy-and-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156865436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2169122636838539824"><i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i> was a pleasant surprise for a number of reasons. I did not expect a great story mostly because in 1902, the Swedish Ministry of Education commissioned Selma Lagerlof to write the adventure as a way to make geography a bit more entertaining for school children. As a result, I thought the didactic purpose behind the book would result in a didactic story.<br/><br/>It was anything but! This is an entertaining story. I did not know the location of places where the adventure tak</span>
  <span id="freeText2169122636838539824" style="display:none"><i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i> was a pleasant surprise for a number of reasons. I did not expect a great story mostly because in 1902, the Swedish Ministry of Education commissioned Selma Lagerlof to write the adventure as a way to make geography a bit more entertaining for school children. As a result, I thought the didactic purpose behind the book would result in a didactic story.<br /><br />It was anything but! This is an entertaining story. I did not know the location of places where the adventure takes place. Those who do not know Swedish geography should not let their ignorance dissuade them from a great read. It might help to have a map to look at.<br /><br />The story is a morality tale. What is a morality tale? It's many things and often involves a change of heart in a key character, who was once bad, is pulled into an adventure, realizes the errors of his/her ways and turns good.<br /><br />In the Lagerlof story, the chief delight of Nils Holgersson, the boy who forms the center of the work, is to eat and sleep, and after that he likes to make mischief. He takes great delight in hurting the animals on his family's farm. After an elf shrinks Nils into a small person who is able to talk with animals, they are thrilled to see the boy reduced to their size. While this is happening, wild geese are flying over the farm on a migration north for the spring, and a white farm goose attempts to join the wild ones. In an attempt to salvage something before his family returns, Nils holds on to the bird's neck as it successfully takes off and joins the wild birds. Off Nils goes on his adventure across Sweden.<br /><br />Knowing that a book is a morality take would prevent many from reading "The Wonderful Adventure of Nils," but this is a good morality tale in part because it is so entertaining. There is danger--mostly from a fox and crows--enchantment and the slow maturation of Nils from a uncouth ruffian into a man.<br /><br />I especially liked two sections, including one where Nils, one night in a grotto on the sea, discovers a mystically beautiful city. It's a vision of Plato's Golden City. After visiting the city, Nils goes to fetch a friend to show him Elysium, but he discovers that he cannot return to the city. He receives a one-time vision of perfection. Despondent by his loss of paradise, Nils is flown by the geese over a real, dilapidated city, and the boy realizes something: It's better that the mystical city of perfection is shown to only a few fortunates so that it doesn't decay like a real city would. Moreover, the brief vision of perfection can serve as a guidepost to Nils for life in a world that mirrors the dilapidated city.<br /><br />I also loved a section where Nils discovers an old peasant woman, who has been abandoned by her children. It's incredibly sad and makes Nils realize how blessed he is. I plan to return to that section in the future when I get down.<br /><br />Many 20th Century fantasy works emerged from the UK, including those by George McDonald, JRR Tolkien, CS Lewis and others. I enjoyed <i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i> in part because the story emerged from outside the English-speaking world. Central Europe's fantasy tradition, via ETA Hoffman, the Grimm Bros. and others, is a bit older than Western Europe's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2169122636838539824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2165208282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165208282" />
    <a title="Michael Haase" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36432305-michael-haase"><img alt="Michael Haase" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498749694p2/36432305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2165208282?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Haase" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Haase" href="/user/show/36432305-michael-haase">Michael Haase</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/23274295-nils-holgerssons-underbara-resa-genom-sverige">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165208282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5848161270679133505">If you see low ratings and bad reviews for this novel, it's perhaps because those readers had expected an entertaining children's parable like Pinocchio or Hans Anderson's fables, but this book is nothing like those. It reads more like a travel guide than a fairy tale. That doesn't necessarily mean it isn't good in its own right. <br/><br/>The emphasis of the book is not on <i>Nils Holgersson</i> but on the <i>journey through Sweden</i> aspect. Throughout the text, the reader is brought with Nils on a trip to the diffe</span>
  <span id="freeText5848161270679133505" style="display:none">If you see low ratings and bad reviews for this novel, it's perhaps because those readers had expected an entertaining children's parable like Pinocchio or Hans Anderson's fables, but this book is nothing like those. It reads more like a travel guide than a fairy tale. That doesn't necessarily mean it isn't good in its own right. <br /><br />The emphasis of the book is not on <i>Nils Holgersson</i> but on the <i>journey through Sweden</i> aspect. Throughout the text, the reader is brought with Nils on a trip to the different towns and provinces of old Sweden, depicted with outstanding detail. It's clear that Lagerlöf had a profound admiration for her country and wanted to portray it in all of its splendor. Therefore, the reader can expect to learn much of the customs, architecture, history, and landscape of the nation, and this makes the book a perfect introduction to Sweden and Svenska for those studying the language.<br /><br />The downside to this is the book isn't very amusing to read. It doesn't have the surprise and magical wonder of other Children's stories from that time. I didn't find it particularly captivating or the slightest bit humorous, though I must admit, I was greatly impressed with Lagerlöf's understanding of Swedish particulars, and enjoyed reading the book because of my fascination with Sweden.<br /><br />The tone <i>is</i> extremely lighthearted, filled with praise for the rustic life and love for nature and mankind. It fits in with pastoral texts from earlier times which professed a passion for simple farmstead lifestyle. It reminded me a lot of the Quebecois novel, <i>Marie Chapdelaine</i>. It is optimistic and provides a contrast to the texts of today which are painfully grim and cynical. Nevertheless, I wouldn't consider it a great book to read to kids. This is a text solely for people interested in learning about Sweden. It's one of those books that is rooted in locale, such as <i>Deutschland, ein Wintermärchen</i> and <i>Berlin Alexanderplatz</i>, all of which supply a wealth of information about their settings, but certainly would be boring to anyone who wasn't studying those places concerned.<br /> <br />One last thing to mention, there was an unexpected scene where Lagerlöf herself shows up and saves Nils from an owl, which leads to him describing his journey to her so that she could write it down. It's sort of like a belated acknowledgement passage, since she talks so much about her family. I just thought this kind of scene was sort of abrupt and out of nowhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5848161270679133505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_292035617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292035617" />
    <a title="Sylvia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7408130-sylvia"><img alt="Sylvia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508786698p2/7408130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292035617?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylvia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvia" href="/user/show/7408130-sylvia">Sylvia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9023000579" href="/book/show/11566656-niels-holgerssons-wonderbare-reis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7408130-sylvia?shelf=young-readers">young-readers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7408130-sylvia?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7408130-sylvia?shelf=challenge-2012">challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7408130-sylvia?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer292035617&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292035617" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5955155813839569838">Fairy tales, myths and legends and the beautiful description of the landscape of Sweden, that's all included in this phenomenal book. Together with Niels Holgerson and the wild geese the reader makes a long journey from the south of Sweden to the land of the Sami people. There are many ancient Swedish folktales and legends, stories about animals and their habitat and tales about Sweden as the land develops itself to an industrial nation. <br/><br/>It wasn't the first time I read it. Year ago I used to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText5955155813839569838" style="display:none">Fairy tales, myths and legends and the beautiful description of the landscape of Sweden, that's all included in this phenomenal book. Together with Niels Holgerson and the wild geese the reader makes a long journey from the south of Sweden to the land of the Sami people. There are many ancient Swedish folktales and legends, stories about animals and their habitat and tales about Sweden as the land develops itself to an industrial nation. <br /><br />It wasn't the first time I read it. Year ago I used to read for my school kids, but because time to read is limited during a school year I don't think I have finished it. <br /><br />The tales are - when looking at it from our point of view - moralistic. Niels is a very unruly boy, who is punished for this behavior by a little gnome. He is turned into a hobgoblin and leaves his house with a tame goose and a bunch of wild geese. During his journey he learns to develop good virtues. All is well, that ends well, when he returns with the tame goose and shows to be loyal to their friendship, when his parents want to kill the goose. The moment he steps into the room to keep his parents from killing his friend, the spell is broken and he turned into a normal boy again. <br /><br />Being fond of folktales, fairy tales, myths, legends and fantasy stories I loved to re-read it after so many years. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5955155813839569838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8678567288252117968">Written by Nobel winning Swedish author Selma Lagerlöf about one young boy's journey across Sweden with various animal friends, this parable is truly one for all ages. Through the didactic (and at times socially critical) tour of her country, I learnt of Sweden's historical and industrial national treasures, their proud and rustic sensibility, and the belief in betterment through experience and empathy. The anthropomorphic animals are so realistically tailored, and I loved how I could always fin</span>
  <span id="freeText8678567288252117968" style="display:none">Written by Nobel winning Swedish author Selma Lagerlöf about one young boy's journey across Sweden with various animal friends, this parable is truly one for all ages. Through the didactic (and at times socially critical) tour of her country, I learnt of Sweden's historical and industrial national treasures, their proud and rustic sensibility, and the belief in betterment through experience and empathy. The anthropomorphic animals are so realistically tailored, and I loved how I could always find more reason to laugh at their deft characterisation! So worth the read! I read this in Chinese, but it's worth it in any language. I find children's books to be wonderful, with such sweet lessons to be gleaned from their tales!</span>

<div id="review_3485728246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3485728246" />
    <a title="Mary B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47621821-mary-b"><img alt="Mary B." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3485728246?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary B." href="/user/show/47621821-mary-b">Mary B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18880657-the-wonderful-adventures-of-nils">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3485728246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14407120916549398985">When Selma Lagerlöf began crafting The Wonderful Adventures of Nils, she sought to create an engaging novel that would help school children learn about the geography and culture of Sweden. Along the way, she created a beautiful and enduring piece of work with deep meaning for all cultures and generations.<br/><br/>Blending myth, fable, folk tale and fantasy, Lagerlöf masterfully infuses lessons about geography, animal life, environmental stewardship, friendship, responsibility and kindness into her highly</span>
  <span id="freeText14407120916549398985" style="display:none">When Selma Lagerlöf began crafting The Wonderful Adventures of Nils, she sought to create an engaging novel that would help school children learn about the geography and culture of Sweden. Along the way, she created a beautiful and enduring piece of work with deep meaning for all cultures and generations.<br /><br />Blending myth, fable, folk tale and fantasy, Lagerlöf masterfully infuses lessons about geography, animal life, environmental stewardship, friendship, responsibility and kindness into her highly imaginative, captivating tale. Marked by its lyrical language, vivid imagery and soulfulness, the story follows the adventures of a boy who, after being turned into an elf, explores Sweden while riding on the back of a goose. Along the way, he comes to understand the richness, diversity and beauty of his homeland and the importance of caring for the world and all its creatures, human or otherwise.<br /><br />In 1909, Lagerlöf won the Nobel Prize in literature for The Wonderful Adventures of Nils. She was the first woman to receive this honor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14407120916549398985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_42318'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42318.Karlsson_on_the_Roof"><img alt="Karlsson on the Roof" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1207091552l/42318._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ue/SljA4Pca8ixFB5gb7g7b8uRwyGc3Te90FnB/ciiiGsv2Uara/LkCI2jbny54WNuWGwBsFZ9/iMLA9R+5B6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x06aIaHinOtZDejOMrAVqo8d7jhJVciE9PUS51A8gIQQE7Uj+2weA6UOI7kzfXA/DwTR5GBJYohtGKdGCA5LRw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38266.Selma_Lagerl_f">About Selma Lagerlöf</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38266.Selma_Lagerl_f"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1237932710p3/38266.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/38266.Selma_Lagerl_f">Selma Lagerlöf

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4893267837282926899">Selma Ottilia Lovisa Lagerlöf (1858-1940) was a Swedish author. In 1909 she became the first woman to ever receive the Nobel Prize in Literature, "in appreciation of the lofty idealism, vivid imagination and spiritual perception that characterize her writings". She later also became the first female member of the Swedish Academy. <br/><br/>Born in the forested countryside of Sweden she was told many of the </span>
  <span id="freeText4893267837282926899" style="display:none">Selma Ottilia Lovisa Lagerlöf (1858-1940) was a Swedish author. In 1909 she became the first woman to ever receive the Nobel Prize in Literature, "in appreciation of the lofty idealism, vivid imagination and spiritual perception that characterize her writings". She later also became the first female member of the Swedish Academy. <br /><br />Born in the forested countryside of Sweden she was told many of the classic Swedish fairytales, which she would later use as inspiration in her magic realist writings. Since she for some of her early years had problems with her legs (she was born with a faulty hip) she would also spend a lot of time reading books such as the Bible.<br /><br />As a young woman she was a teacher in the southern parts of Sweden for ten years before her first novel <i>Gösta Berling's Saga</i> was published. As her writer career progressed she would keep up a correspondance with some of her former female collegues for almost her entire life. <br /><br />Lagerlöf never married and was almost certainly a lesbian (she never officially stated that she was, but most later researchers believe this to be the case). For many years her constant companion was fellow writer Sophie Elkan, with whom she traveled to Italy and the Middle East. Her visit to Palestine and a colony of Christians there, would inspire her to write <i>Jerusalem</i>, her story of Swedish farmers converting into a evangelical Christian group and travelling to "The American Colony" in Jerusalem.<br /><br />Lagerlöf was involved in both women issues as well as politics. She would among other things help the Jewish writer Nelly Sachs to come to Sweden and donated her Nobel medal to the Finnish war effort against the Soviet union. <br /><br />Outside of Sweden she's perhaps most widely known for her children's book <i>Nils Holgerssons underbara resa genom Sverige</i> (<i>The Wonderful Adventures of Nils</i>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4893267837282926899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
